<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">Mariah Carey albums discography</span></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p>American singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> has released fourteen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio albums</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack_album" title="Soundtrack album">soundtrack album</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Live_album" title="Live album">live album</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation albums</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a>, and one <a href="/wiki/Remix_album" title="Remix album">remix album</a>. Carey is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists of all-time</a>, having sold over 200 million records globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presstoyounow_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-presstoyounow-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presstoyou_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-presstoyou-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sales_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-sales-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> She was presented with the <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards#Millennium_Awards" title="World Music Awards">Millennium Award</a> at the 2000 <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a> for becoming the best-selling female artist of the millennium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the RIAA, she is the third best-selling female artist and sixteenth overall recording artist with shipments of 63.5 million albums in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa.com_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaa.com-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariah_Marks_Milestone_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mariah_Marks_Milestone-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> She is also ranked as the best-selling female artist of the US <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era (from 1991) with album sales of 54 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chanteuse_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-chanteuse-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Her albums <i><a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey_(album)" title="Mariah Carey (album)">Mariah Carey</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Box_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Music Box (Mariah Carey album)">Music Box</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Daydream_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Daydream (Mariah Carey album)">Daydream</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emancipation_of_Mimi" title="The Emancipation of Mimi">The Emancipation of Mimi</a></i> are among the top 100 certified albums according to the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey released her <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey_(album)" title="Mariah Carey (album)">self-titled</a> debut album in June 1990; it was certified nine-times <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAA_certifications" title="RIAA certifications">Platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), denoting shipments of nine million copies in the United States. Additionally, the album spawned four consecutive US number-one singles. Her second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey album)">Emotions</a></i>, was released a year later and sold eight million copies worldwide. In 1993, Carey released her most successful studio album to date, <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Box_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Music Box (Mariah Carey album)">Music Box</a></i>, which was certified Diamond in the United States and topped the charts in many countries around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaa-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Music Box</i> is one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_worldwide" title="List of best-selling albums worldwide">best-selling albums</a> of all time, with over 32 million copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-List_of_Best_Selling_Albums_.28Page_9.29_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-List_of_Best_Selling_Albums_.28Page_9.29-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1994 Carey released her first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holiday_album" title="Holiday album">holiday album</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Merry Christmas (Mariah Carey album)">Merry Christmas</a></i>, containing the worldwide Christmas classic "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_I_Want_for_Christmas_Is_You_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="All I Want for Christmas Is You (Mariah Carey song)">All I Want for Christmas Is You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prnewswire1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> After Carey's success in Asia with <i>Merry Christmas</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> estimated Carey as the all time best-selling international artist in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1995, Carey released her fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Daydream_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Daydream (Mariah Carey album)">Daydream</a></i>, which became her second Diamond certified album by the RIAA, with worldwide sales of 25 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bet_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-bet-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey's fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Butterfly_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Butterfly (Mariah Carey album)">Butterfly</a></i>, and the compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Number_1%27s_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Number 1's (Mariah Carey album)">#1's</a></i>, were both certified five-times Platinum in the US; the latter remains the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_Japan" title="List of best-selling albums in Japan">best-selling album in Japan</a> by a non-Asian artist, selling 3.25 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariah_Carey_.231.27s_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mariah_Carey_.231.27s-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rainbow_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Rainbow (Mariah Carey album)">Rainbow</a></i> (1999), Carey's sixth studio effort, received triple platinum certification from RIAA. But it was her first album since <i>Emotions</i> to not reach number one in the US. In 2001 Carey parted from Columbia/Sony Music and signed a contract with EMI's <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Records" title="Virgin Records">Virgin Records</a> worth a reported US$100 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mayer_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mayer-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> the largest record contract ever signed. She released her next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Glitter_(soundtrack)" title="Glitter (soundtrack)">Glitter</a></i>, which was the <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack_album" title="Soundtrack album">soundtrack</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Glitter_(film)" title="Glitter (film)">film of same name</a>. The album suffered from poor publicity and became a commercial failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fox_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-fox-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey signed a new deal in 2002 with <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island Records</a> and released her seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Charmbracelet" title="Charmbracelet">Charmbracelet</a></i>; the album still failed short of Carey's earlier success. The singer then took a three year break to record new material and introduced a hip-hop inspired album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emancipation_of_Mimi" title="The Emancipation of Mimi">The Emancipation of Mimi</a></i>, which became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best-selling_albums_by_year_in_the_United_States" title="Best-selling albums by year in the United States">best-selling album of 2005</a> in the US. It was certified six-times Platinum by the RIAA, sold twelve million copies worldwide, and produced the successful single "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/We_Belong_Together_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="We Belong Together (Mariah Carey song)">We Belong Together</a>", it topped the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for fourteen weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, Carey released her ninth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/E%3DMC%C2%B2_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="E=MC² (Mariah Carey album)">E=MC²</a></i>, which sold over 2.5 million copies worldwide and produced the single "<a href="/wiki/Touch_My_Body_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Touch My Body (Mariah Carey song)">Touch My Body</a>" which broke her tie with <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> for the most number one singles by a solo artist on the Hot 100. Her subsequent release, <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i> (2009), managed sales of two million units,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memoirssales_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-memoirssales-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> while her second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holiday_album" title="Holiday album">holiday album</a> <a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_II_You" title="Merry Christmas II You">Merry Christmas II You</a> (2010) shipped over 500,000 copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-askbillboard_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-askbillboard-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The singer's fourteenth effort, <i><a href="/wiki/Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse" title="Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse">Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse</a></i>, failed commercially, becoming the lowest selling release of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presstoyounow_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-presstoyounow-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chanteuse_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-chanteuse-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>
